<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Settlement of the Americas</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Continents" title="Continents">continents</a> of <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">North and South America</a> were settled by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">natives</a> from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> between 10 and 20 thousand years ago after they crossed a <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a> that formed between <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and far northeastern <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> due to the lowering of sea level during the <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Maximum" title="Last Glacial Maximum">last ice age</a>. Available scientific evidence indicates that <a href="/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans" title="Recent African origin of modern humans">modern humans emerged from Africa</a> over 100,000 years ago, yet did not arrive in the Americas until less than 20,000 years ago. Current understanding of the <b>settlement of the Americas</b> derives from advances in four interrelated disciplines: <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Physical_anthropology" title="Physical anthropology">physical anthropology</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DNA_analysis" title="DNA analysis">DNA analysis</a>. While there is general agreement that the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> were first settled from Asia, the pattern of migration, its timing, and the place(s) of origin in Asia of the peoples who migrated to the Americas remain unclear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goebel_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goebel-1">[1]</a></sup> In the 2000s, researchers sought to use familiar tools to validate or reject established theories, such as <a href="/wiki/Clovis_culture" title="Clovis culture">Clovis first</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">[2]</a></sup> The archeological evidence suggests that the <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleo-Indians</a>' first dispersal into the Americas occurred near the end of the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a> or, more specifically, what is known as the <a href="/wiki/Last_Glacial_Maximum" title="Last Glacial Maximum">Last Glacial Maximum</a> (LGM), around 16,500–13,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goebel_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Goebel-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The settlement of the Americas is of intense interest to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaeologists" title="Archaeologists">archaeologists</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropologists" title="Anthropologists">anthropologists</a>. Modern biochemical techniques, as well as the accumulation of archaeological and geological evidence, have shed progressively more light on the subject; however, significant questions remain unresolved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pauketat2012_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pauketat2012-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
